    >>> import pkgInvoking __init__.py for pkg>>> pkg.A['quux', 'corge', 'grault']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="05b3ed4ba72145a698427352fbc02b82"><span data-offset-key="05b3ed4ba72145a698427352fbc02b82:0">A </span><span data-offset-key="05b3ed4ba72145a698427352fbc02b82:1">**module**</span><span data-offset-key="05b3ed4ba72145a698427352fbc02b82:2"> in the package can access the global variable by importing it in turn:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eaa6004434ec4636b1f173127a1357ab"><span data-offset-key="eaa6004434ec4636b1f173127a1357ab:0">**_mod1.py_**</span></span></span>

    def foo():    from pkg import A    print('[mod1] foo() / A = ', A)​class Foo:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e2349c2c8a5c4ecfad8c7d8d2c57de58"><span data-offset-key="e2349c2c8a5c4ecfad8c7d8d2c57de58:0"> &gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> from pkg import mod1Invoking __init__.py for pkg>>> mod1.foo()[mod1] foo() / A =  ['quux', 'corge', 'grault']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222"><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:0">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:1"> can also be used to effect automatic importing of modules from a package. For example, earlier you saw that the statement </span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:2">`import pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:3"> only places the name </span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:4">`pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:5"> in the caller’s local symbol table and doesn’t import any modules. But if </span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:6">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:7"> in the </span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:8">`pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="c1c1b0d83ac644e991b1c2b93fed6222:9"> directory contains the following:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3146532a232e4cc8a18f521d6be55008"><span data-offset-key="3146532a232e4cc8a18f521d6be55008:0">**_\_\_init\_\_.py_**</span></span></span>

    print(f'Invoking __init__.py for {__name__}')import pkg.mod1, pkg.mod2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033"><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:0">then when you execute </span><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:1">`import pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:2">, modules </span><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:3">`mod1`</span><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:5">`mod2`</span><span data-offset-key="7d417d47fbc843bc905fa949f04c6033:6"> are imported automatically:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> import pkgInvoking __init__.py for pkg>>> pkg.mod1.foo()[mod1] foo()>>> pkg.mod2.bar()[mod2] bar()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96"><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:0">**Note:**</span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:1"> Much of the Python documentation states that an </span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:2">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:3"> file </span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:4">**must**</span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:5"> be present in the package directory when creating a package. This was once true. It used to be that the very presence of </span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:6">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:7"> signified to Python that a package was being defined. The file could contain initialization code or even be empty, but it </span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:8">**had**</span><span data-offset-key="f381301542154187a6ce9ed5bcb2ac96:9"> to be present.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f38f9c7bbdb9434eb37a5c909f80273e"><span data-offset-key="f38f9c7bbdb9434eb37a5c909f80273e:0">Starting with </span><span data-offset-key="f38f9c7bbdb9434eb37a5c909f80273e:1">**Python 3.3**</span><span data-offset-key="f38f9c7bbdb9434eb37a5c909f80273e:2">, </span></span><a href="https://www.python.org/dev/peps/pep-0420" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4b0562617e2f45fbabd2a13c73fadb70"><span data-offset-key="4b0562617e2f45fbabd2a13c73fadb70:0">Implicit Namespace Packages</span></span></a><span data-key="f0d07dc351724bf3856e393892d0877d"><span data-offset-key="f0d07dc351724bf3856e393892d0877d:0"> were introduced. These allow for the creation of a package without any </span><span data-offset-key="f0d07dc351724bf3856e393892d0877d:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="f0d07dc351724bf3856e393892d0877d:2"> file. Of course, it </span><span data-offset-key="f0d07dc351724bf3856e393892d0877d:3">**can**</span><span data-offset-key="f0d07dc351724bf3856e393892d0877d:4"> still be present if package initialization is needed. But it is no longer required.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5c53779cbf504905b49bae7e819612f3"><span data-offset-key="5c53779cbf504905b49bae7e819612f3:0">Importing </span><span data-offset-key="5c53779cbf504905b49bae7e819612f3:1">`*`</span><span data-offset-key="5c53779cbf504905b49bae7e819612f3:2"> From a Package</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="829ae10e1b1b4dea8226d5e2329956bf"><span data-offset-key="829ae10e1b1b4dea8226d5e2329956bf:0">For the purposes of the following discussion, the previously defined package is expanded to contain some additional modules:</span></span><a href="https://files.realpython.com/media/pkg3.d2160908ae77.png" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ba0fa09c15ec4b27b71bc1c0fdf9b805"><span data-offset-key="ba0fa09c15ec4b27b71bc1c0fdf9b805:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><span data-slate-void="true" data-key="3c6a00ca33b94399b4609a0bc08ceb37"><span><span class="reset-3c756112--frameInlineVoid-73b6a96b" data-key="3c6a00ca33b94399b4609a0bc08ceb37"><img src="https://files.realpython.com/media/pkg3.d2160908ae77.png" alt="Illustration of hierarchical file structure of Python packages" class="image-67b14f24--image-54d049be" /></span></span></span><span data-key="e8a1071f05404f06a7bb5c8f26a0a36d"><span data-offset-key="e8a1071f05404f06a7bb5c8f26a0a36d:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></a><span data-key="cc6bd8d38d1b464b8be3a2eb8d2e30a2"><span data-offset-key="cc6bd8d38d1b464b8be3a2eb8d2e30a2:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4ddfd287feda40689106cd51f72bc88c"><span data-offset-key="4ddfd287feda40689106cd51f72bc88c:0">There are now four modules defined in the </span><span data-offset-key="4ddfd287feda40689106cd51f72bc88c:1">`pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="4ddfd287feda40689106cd51f72bc88c:2"> directory. Their contents are as shown below:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bcf4e635ef21439ca35faa33cc55fd09"><span data-offset-key="bcf4e635ef21439ca35faa33cc55fd09:0">**_mod1.py_**</span></span></span>

    def foo():    print('[mod1] foo()')​class Foo:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="89284d229377424d9236f9b678a9b489"><span data-offset-key="89284d229377424d9236f9b678a9b489:0">**_mod2.py_**</span></span></span>

    def bar():    print('[mod2] bar()')​class Bar:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fedbafaecee248e5849bc4ad5202ece6"><span data-offset-key="fedbafaecee248e5849bc4ad5202ece6:0">**_mod3.py_**</span></span></span>

    def baz():    print('[mod3] baz()')​class Baz:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a775dca84c404148a0a3d71a1ad49eb8"><span data-offset-key="a775dca84c404148a0a3d71a1ad49eb8:0">**_mod4.py_**</span></span></span>

    def qux():    print('[mod4] qux()')​class Qux:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0f0c9aa62a074509bc17ec068c8dfc54"><span data-offset-key="0f0c9aa62a074509bc17ec068c8dfc54:0">(Imaginative, aren’t they?)</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef"><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:0">You have already seen that when </span><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:1">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:2"> is used for a </span><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:3">**module**</span><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:5">_all_</span><span data-offset-key="d9796dd110ba4d168f55e7cdc73fcbef:6"> objects from the module are imported into the local symbol table, except those whose names begin with an underscore, as always:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__']​>>> from pkg.mod3 import *​>>> dir()['Baz', '__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__', 'baz']>>> baz()[mod3] baz()>>> Baz<class 'pkg.mod3.Baz'>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="05350beb22e940b78e8575a6edea4b71"><span data-offset-key="05350beb22e940b78e8575a6edea4b71:0">The analogous statement for a </span><span data-offset-key="05350beb22e940b78e8575a6edea4b71:1">**package**</span><span data-offset-key="05350beb22e940b78e8575a6edea4b71:2"> is this:</span></span></span>

    from <package_name> import *

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fc975bd0bc2749dd84feb334d9c5d935"><span data-offset-key="fc975bd0bc2749dd84feb334d9c5d935:0">What does that do?&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__']​>>> from pkg import *>>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5230fc9443b8417f8fde92f468173b83"><span data-offset-key="5230fc9443b8417f8fde92f468173b83:0">Hmph. Not much. You might have expected (assuming you had any expectations at all) that Python would dive down into the package directory, find all the modules it could, and import them all. But as you can see, by default that is not what happens.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367"><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:0">Instead, Python follows this convention: if the </span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:2"> file in the </span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:3">**package**</span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:4"> directory contains a </span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:5">**list**</span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:6"> named </span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:7">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:8">, it is taken to be a list of modules that should be imported when the statement </span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:9">`from <package_name> import *`</span><span data-offset-key="1f1a5f629a2b402c95b2226947043367:10"> is encountered.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="490f19af399d4639b7c26aa382df6853"><span data-offset-key="490f19af399d4639b7c26aa382df6853:0">For the present example, suppose you create an </span><span data-offset-key="490f19af399d4639b7c26aa382df6853:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="490f19af399d4639b7c26aa382df6853:2"> in the </span><span data-offset-key="490f19af399d4639b7c26aa382df6853:3">`pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="490f19af399d4639b7c26aa382df6853:4"> directory like this:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3b8daf4198240919053f5f005ec0e7a"><span data-offset-key="a3b8daf4198240919053f5f005ec0e7a:0">**_pkg/\_\_init\_\_.py_**</span></span></span>

    __all__ = [        'mod1',        'mod2',        'mod3',        'mod4'        ]

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e460cb1805f34499aff82bed9e808342"><span data-offset-key="e460cb1805f34499aff82bed9e808342:0">Now </span><span data-offset-key="e460cb1805f34499aff82bed9e808342:1">`from pkg import *`</span><span data-offset-key="e460cb1805f34499aff82bed9e808342:2"> imports all four modules:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__']​>>> from pkg import *>>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__', 'mod1', 'mod2', 'mod3', 'mod4']>>> mod2.bar()[mod2] bar()>>> mod4.Qux<class 'pkg.mod4.Qux'>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97"><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:1">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:2"> still isn’t considered terrific form, any more for </span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:3">**packages**</span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:4"> than for </span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:5">**modules**</span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:6">. But this facility at least gives the creator of the package some control over what happens when </span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:7">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:8"> is specified. (In fact, it provides the capability to disallow it entirely, simply by declining to define </span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:9">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="810641a45e6b48e696f777bcbe151a97:10"> at all. As you have seen, the default behavior for packages is to import nothing.)</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce"><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:0">By the way, </span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:1">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:2"> can be defined in a </span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:3">**module**</span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:4"> as well and serves the same purpose: to control what is imported with </span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:5">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:6">. For example, modify </span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:7">`mod1.py`</span><span data-offset-key="260feff6df9e47bb91d68e30502ce6ce:8"> as follows:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6a62af83a1744db3b107904ab1ff4fce"><span data-offset-key="6a62af83a1744db3b107904ab1ff4fce:0">**_pkg/mod1.py_**</span></span></span>

    __all__ = ['foo']​def foo():    print('[mod1] foo()')​class Foo:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988"><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:0">Now an </span><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:1">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:2"> statement from </span><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:3">`pkg.mod1`</span><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:4"> will only import what is contained in </span><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:5">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="af1f2674faa54dd5b63b33c49583a988:6">:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__']​>>> from pkg.mod1 import *>>> dir()['__annotations__', '__builtins__', '__doc__', '__loader__', '__name__','__package__', '__spec__', 'foo']​>>> foo()[mod1] foo()>>> FooTraceback (most recent call last):  File "<pyshell#37>", line 1, in <module>    FooNameError: name 'Foo' is not defined

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231"><span data-offset-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231:0">`foo()`</span><span data-offset-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231:1"> (the function) is now defined in the local namespace, but </span><span data-offset-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231:2">`Foo`</span><span data-offset-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231:3"> (the class) is not, because the latter is not in </span><span data-offset-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231:4">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="718d25102b6a4b27aa0b4261475ba231:5">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d"><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:0">In summary, </span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:1">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:2"> is used by both </span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:3">**packages**</span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:5">**modules**</span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:6"> to control what is imported when </span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:7">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:8"> is specified. But </span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:9">_the default behavior differs_</span><span data-offset-key="e6ffb288b250458282ff38b5b01c7a8d:10">:</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5f45d6dff343482d87d4976e5bd971ab"><span data-offset-key="5f45d6dff343482d87d4976e5bd971ab:0">For a package, when </span><span data-offset-key="5f45d6dff343482d87d4976e5bd971ab:1">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="5f45d6dff343482d87d4976e5bd971ab:2"> is not defined, </span><span data-offset-key="5f45d6dff343482d87d4976e5bd971ab:3">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="5f45d6dff343482d87d4976e5bd971ab:4"> does not import anything.</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="908683d1b6e5463db270012de8adbc5a"><span data-offset-key="908683d1b6e5463db270012de8adbc5a:0">For a module, when </span><span data-offset-key="908683d1b6e5463db270012de8adbc5a:1">`__all__`</span><span data-offset-key="908683d1b6e5463db270012de8adbc5a:2"> is not defined, </span><span data-offset-key="908683d1b6e5463db270012de8adbc5a:3">`import *`</span><span data-offset-key="908683d1b6e5463db270012de8adbc5a:4"> imports everything (except—you guessed it—names starting with an underscore).</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="900aba14084e44d2b44e9546314bb06f"><span data-offset-key="900aba14084e44d2b44e9546314bb06f:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://srv.realpython.net/click/58257184031/?c=31941813441&amp;p=58946116052&amp;r=17046" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f29a7b17216144e5863448292c31e28f"><span data-offset-key="f29a7b17216144e5863448292c31e28f:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><span data-slate-void="true" data-key="41e05ce21abf4bc3bc03cd9510aa8737"><span><span class="reset-3c756112--frameInlineVoid-73b6a96b" data-key="41e05ce21abf4bc3bc03cd9510aa8737"><img src="https://img.realpython.net/16bf1efe41b538fae54711c58c701f0e" class="image-67b14f24--image-54d049be" /></span></span></span><span data-key="777fe14dd475407e8ff920183e342105"><span data-offset-key="777fe14dd475407e8ff920183e342105:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></a><span data-key="fe4e7c2e49e9446c898aca9f907781b1"><span data-offset-key="fe4e7c2e49e9446c898aca9f907781b1:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://realpython.com/account/join/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4904ea341c4e40e2ba5cfceafdca17a3"><span data-offset-key="4904ea341c4e40e2ba5cfceafdca17a3:0"> Remove ads</span></span></a><span data-key="61f731cf939340c2b5aab3bd031a623e"><span data-offset-key="61f731cf939340c2b5aab3bd031a623e:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3e4b5b785e2e48a9a869524035ecde93"><span data-offset-key="3e4b5b785e2e48a9a869524035ecde93:0">Subpackages</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="62eb6eb4a44f40e58e81dec9f6b58637"><span data-offset-key="62eb6eb4a44f40e58e81dec9f6b58637:0">Packages can contain nested </span><span data-offset-key="62eb6eb4a44f40e58e81dec9f6b58637:1">**subpackages**</span><span data-offset-key="62eb6eb4a44f40e58e81dec9f6b58637:2"> to arbitrary depth. For example, let’s make one more modification to the example </span><span data-offset-key="62eb6eb4a44f40e58e81dec9f6b58637:3">**package**</span><span data-offset-key="62eb6eb4a44f40e58e81dec9f6b58637:4"> directory as follows:</span></span><a href="https://files.realpython.com/media/pkg4.a830d6e144bf.png" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f917a5ff6671445f9640fddbd0a36e95"><span data-offset-key="f917a5ff6671445f9640fddbd0a36e95:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><span data-slate-void="true" data-key="223f9a7903d94194bd9dada56c782a74"><span><span class="reset-3c756112--frameInlineVoid-73b6a96b" data-key="223f9a7903d94194bd9dada56c782a74"><img src="https://files.realpython.com/media/pkg4.a830d6e144bf.png" alt="Illustration of hierarchical file structure of Python packages" class="image-67b14f24--image-54d049be" /></span></span></span><span data-key="2b5b9a2691ca4d1cbf0f4d8539d40305"><span data-offset-key="2b5b9a2691ca4d1cbf0f4d8539d40305:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></a><span data-key="4e1d7e701147431f9422447d2bd5e7fa"><span data-offset-key="4e1d7e701147431f9422447d2bd5e7fa:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a"><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:0">The four modules (</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:1">`mod1.py`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:3">`mod2.py`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:4">, </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:5">`mod3.py`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:6"> and </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:7">`mod4.py`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:8">) are defined as previously. But now, instead of being lumped together into the </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:9">`pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:10"> directory, they are split out into two </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:11">**subpackage**</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:12"> directories, </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:13">`sub_pkg1`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:14"> and </span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:15">`sub_pkg2`</span><span data-offset-key="77b0f02e6b604f07a13dfc04b99f6d3a:16">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa"><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:0">Importing still works the same as shown previously. Syntax is similar, but additional </span><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:1">**dot notation**</span><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:2"> is used to separate </span><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:3">**package**</span><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:4"> name from </span><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:5">**subpackage**</span><span data-offset-key="78a533ebc16347ce9f87281622b5a4fa:6"> name:&gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> import pkg.sub_pkg1.mod1>>> pkg.sub_pkg1.mod1.foo()[mod1] foo()​>>> from pkg.sub_pkg1 import mod2>>> mod2.bar()[mod2] bar()​>>> from pkg.sub_pkg2.mod3 import baz>>> baz()[mod3] baz()​>>> from pkg.sub_pkg2.mod4 import qux as grault>>> grault()[mod4] qux()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255"><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:0">In addition, a module in one </span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:1">**subpackage**</span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:2"> can reference objects in a </span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:3">**sibling subpackage**</span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:4"> (in the event that the sibling contains some functionality that you need). For example, suppose you want to import and execute function </span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:5">`foo()`</span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:6"> (defined in module </span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:7">`mod1`</span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:8">) from within module </span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:9">`mod3`</span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:10">. You can either use an </span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:11">**absolute import**</span><span data-offset-key="1b6387489ab94f4895eec47b5799c255:12">:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c3e46e92daa940d4980f437fd5912ae3"><span data-offset-key="c3e46e92daa940d4980f437fd5912ae3:0">**_pkg/sub\_\_pkg2/mod3.py_**</span></span></span>

    def baz():    print('[mod3] baz()')​class Baz:    pass​from pkg.sub_pkg1.mod1 import foofoo()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="24612325744142efb3fbff853d53d714"><span data-offset-key="24612325744142efb3fbff853d53d714:0"> &gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> from pkg.sub_pkg2 import mod3[mod1] foo()>>> mod3.foo()[mod1] foo()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0"><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:0">Or you can use a </span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:1">**relative import**</span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:2">, where </span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:3">`..`</span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:4"> refers to the package one level up. From within </span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:5">`mod3.py`</span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:6">, which is in subpackage </span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:7">`sub_pkg2`</span><span data-offset-key="dc2030010a584d7c8010a431945b2dd0:8">,</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2a32bf36d4e2493ab9088795f8d68de3"><span data-offset-key="2a32bf36d4e2493ab9088795f8d68de3:0">`..`</span><span data-offset-key="2a32bf36d4e2493ab9088795f8d68de3:1"> evaluates to the parent package (</span><span data-offset-key="2a32bf36d4e2493ab9088795f8d68de3:2">`pkg`</span><span data-offset-key="2a32bf36d4e2493ab9088795f8d68de3:3">), and</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b67494c099fb4c09a19cdbd186bd4752"><span data-offset-key="b67494c099fb4c09a19cdbd186bd4752:0">`..sub_pkg1`</span><span data-offset-key="b67494c099fb4c09a19cdbd186bd4752:1"> evaluates to subpackage </span><span data-offset-key="b67494c099fb4c09a19cdbd186bd4752:2">`sub_pkg1`</span><span data-offset-key="b67494c099fb4c09a19cdbd186bd4752:3"> of the parent package.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="392a29e35ba841dfa2ddfe9d48f79ce2"><span data-offset-key="392a29e35ba841dfa2ddfe9d48f79ce2:0">**_pkg/sub\_\_pkg2/mod3.py_**</span></span></span>

    def baz():    print('[mod3] baz()')​class Baz:    pass​from .. import sub_pkg1print(sub_pkg1)​from ..sub_pkg1.mod1 import foofoo()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="87f051bfa9544ef7980af6182857c265"><span data-offset-key="87f051bfa9544ef7980af6182857c265:0"> &gt;&gt;&gt;</span></span></span>

    >>> from pkg.sub_pkg2 import mod3<module 'pkg.sub_pkg1' (namespace)>[mod1] foo()

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c046c493508e4f168b7096e1bcd055ca"><span data-offset-key="c046c493508e4f168b7096e1bcd055ca:0">Conclusion</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3a8dd3b5e8db4ea2a9f605f294f7abbb"><span data-offset-key="3a8dd3b5e8db4ea2a9f605f294f7abbb:0">In this tutorial, you covered the following topics:</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="76f02ca8040f4d2c98ae85beeeae0190"><span data-offset-key="76f02ca8040f4d2c98ae85beeeae0190:0">How to create a Python </span><span data-offset-key="76f02ca8040f4d2c98ae85beeeae0190:1">**module**</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4f22202c42374c83a2a253356967b668"><span data-offset-key="4f22202c42374c83a2a253356967b668:0">Locations where the Python interpreter searches for a module</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c0484ae2fb5245b197b420caa419a8e1"><span data-offset-key="c0484ae2fb5245b197b420caa419a8e1:0">How to obtain access to the objects defined in a module with the </span><span data-offset-key="c0484ae2fb5245b197b420caa419a8e1:1">`import`</span><span data-offset-key="c0484ae2fb5245b197b420caa419a8e1:2"> statement</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3f9983e0c9274e3ba67be9862e358072"><span data-offset-key="3f9983e0c9274e3ba67be9862e358072:0">How to create a module that is executable as a standalone script</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ce83a5d02124827bb563e489b274dda"><span data-offset-key="0ce83a5d02124827bb563e489b274dda:0">How to organize modules into </span><span data-offset-key="0ce83a5d02124827bb563e489b274dda:1">**packages**</span><span data-offset-key="0ce83a5d02124827bb563e489b274dda:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="0ce83a5d02124827bb563e489b274dda:3">**subpackages**</span></span></span>

- <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b512314a5146427fa3744d04b6af15a0"><span data-offset-key="b512314a5146427fa3744d04b6af15a0:0">How to control package initialization</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a5305c9c2c0b42dab4e8039a4ad2e484"><span data-offset-key="a5305c9c2c0b42dab4e8039a4ad2e484:0">**Free PDF Download:**</span><span data-offset-key="a5305c9c2c0b42dab4e8039a4ad2e484:1"> </span></span><a href="https://realpython.com/bonus/python-cheat-sheet-short/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="de2e17d874c84a098e563c63e95541b4"><span data-offset-key="de2e17d874c84a098e563c63e95541b4:0">Python 3 Cheat Sheet</span></span></a><span data-key="0b91ad4da2c843a694b107edc5110506"><span data-offset-key="0b91ad4da2c843a694b107edc5110506:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9ac20f122aae495d97dad14f622f4028"><span data-offset-key="9ac20f122aae495d97dad14f622f4028:0">This will hopefully allow you to better understand how to gain access to the functionality available in the many third-party and built-in modules available in Python.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6f6a3b54485d43aaa431bf57e7b4fa65"><span data-offset-key="6f6a3b54485d43aaa431bf57e7b4fa65:0">Additionally, if you are developing your own application, creating your own </span><span data-offset-key="6f6a3b54485d43aaa431bf57e7b4fa65:1">**modules**</span><span data-offset-key="6f6a3b54485d43aaa431bf57e7b4fa65:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="6f6a3b54485d43aaa431bf57e7b4fa65:3">**packages**</span><span data-offset-key="6f6a3b54485d43aaa431bf57e7b4fa65:4"> will help you organize and modularize your code, which makes coding, maintenance, and debugging easier.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe9befa636be45f48951ded0742db245"><span data-offset-key="fe9befa636be45f48951ded0742db245:0">If you want to learn more, check out the following documentation at </span><span data-offset-key="fe9befa636be45f48951ded0742db245:1">**Python.org**</span><span data-offset-key="fe9befa636be45f48951ded0742db245:2">:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6a28ebcb3c7f480c85af420f58aa7ab6"><span data-offset-key="6a28ebcb3c7f480c85af420f58aa7ab6:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="23f9bafea0084156aec3ade4d215bb7b"><span data-offset-key="23f9bafea0084156aec3ade4d215bb7b:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d5330759c292403494c62f451ed94ecf"><span data-offset-key="d5330759c292403494c62f451ed94ecf:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ce38ea6a067485594552cfea1d32974"><span data-offset-key="0ce38ea6a067485594552cfea1d32974:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH700-04e1a2a3--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1b525b1ea6dc48b0ae3106412a63a936"><span data-offset-key="1b525b1ea6dc48b0ae3106412a63a936:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/__main__.html#module-__main__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="89342d4fd71d4789b4f1d9b91196315b"><span data-offset-key="89342d4fd71d4789b4f1d9b91196315b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**main**</code></span></span></a><span data-key="582307860afa4f6ebba6cf5685d1e120"><span data-offset-key="582307860afa4f6ebba6cf5685d1e120:0"> — Top-level script environment</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9b21af6f9fdf47d98d9b8490e8ec78e0"><span data-offset-key="9b21af6f9fdf47d98d9b8490e8ec78e0:0">`'__main__'`</span><span data-offset-key="9b21af6f9fdf47d98d9b8490e8ec78e0:1"> is the name of the scope in which top-level code executes. A module’s \_\_name\_\_ is set equal to </span><span data-offset-key="9b21af6f9fdf47d98d9b8490e8ec78e0:2">`'__main__'`</span><span data-offset-key="9b21af6f9fdf47d98d9b8490e8ec78e0:3"> when read from standard input, a script, or from an interactive prompt.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="541e411e85d54c45ac3e372d830df6f6"><span data-offset-key="541e411e85d54c45ac3e372d830df6f6:0">A module can discover whether or not it is running in the main scope by checking its own </span><span data-offset-key="541e411e85d54c45ac3e372d830df6f6:1">`__name__`</span><span data-offset-key="541e411e85d54c45ac3e372d830df6f6:2">, which allows a common idiom for conditionally executing code in a module when it is run as a script or with </span><span data-offset-key="541e411e85d54c45ac3e372d830df6f6:3">`python -m`</span><span data-offset-key="541e411e85d54c45ac3e372d830df6f6:4"> but not when it is imported:</span></span></span>

    if __name__ == "__main__":    # execute only if run as a script    main()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="940c076f6ccb416c883512426a322c1f"><span data-offset-key="940c076f6ccb416c883512426a322c1f:0">For a package, the same effect can be achieved by including a </span><span data-offset-key="940c076f6ccb416c883512426a322c1f:1">`__main__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="940c076f6ccb416c883512426a322c1f:2"> module, the contents of which will be executed when the module is run</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3fca35a04d3048418645f8f8578ae65a"><span data-offset-key="3fca35a04d3048418645f8f8578ae65a:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0b373cbe037b493d9b59409502ff4e1a"><span data-offset-key="0b373cbe037b493d9b59409502ff4e1a:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a72bc83ac9b248cb9f5ab999f13cd68c"><span data-offset-key="a72bc83ac9b248cb9f5ab999f13cd68c:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="n">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH700-04e1a2a3--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="aef2f48e634b451ca234f0c69b93e9ad"><span data-offset-key="aef2f48e634b451ca234f0c69b93e9ad:0">. The import system</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b95f216b3dda4fc18e7d8556afd43f69"><span data-offset-key="b95f216b3dda4fc18e7d8556afd43f69:0">Python code in one </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-module" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="24ad9ef9bd754e99ab496324a52194e7"><span data-offset-key="24ad9ef9bd754e99ab496324a52194e7:0">module</span></span></a><span data-key="b822d02b28644fb89c9f0fc0f662e9fd"><span data-offset-key="b822d02b28644fb89c9f0fc0f662e9fd:0"> gains access to the code in another module by the process of </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-importing" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8f8d0946a4cc491d9b322accee2af56a"><span data-offset-key="8f8d0946a4cc491d9b322accee2af56a:0">importing</span></span></a><span data-key="7341c1c77e884b5f84bcf8ffe303f242"><span data-offset-key="7341c1c77e884b5f84bcf8ffe303f242:0"> it. The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2da5c4c0f7de4543964ed4626028aaa1"><span data-offset-key="2da5c4c0f7de4543964ed4626028aaa1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7196c549ae9f430a84d6e6bd29de1063"><span data-offset-key="7196c549ae9f430a84d6e6bd29de1063:0"> statement is the most common way of invoking the import machinery, but it is not the only way. Functions such as </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#importlib.import_module" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="130ff7e6a9e248d5a75e69e736da39d0"><span data-offset-key="130ff7e6a9e248d5a75e69e736da39d0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib.import_module()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b7a45853252245d294130b016bafa809"><span data-offset-key="b7a45853252245d294130b016bafa809:0"> and built-in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e718d90a09bd43e3a046bab79828dacd"><span data-offset-key="e718d90a09bd43e3a046bab79828dacd:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0a862ee013a94cb4b076ec4b9e672cdc"><span data-offset-key="0a862ee013a94cb4b076ec4b9e672cdc:0"> can also be used to invoke the import machinery.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="17bcc5fdf9924e7bbd4d42ac1e3a876c"><span data-offset-key="17bcc5fdf9924e7bbd4d42ac1e3a876c:0">The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="38ca1384a05f4a8abce02a7be1a2673b"><span data-offset-key="38ca1384a05f4a8abce02a7be1a2673b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b687c57b822b479b92c23864ae514744"><span data-offset-key="b687c57b822b479b92c23864ae514744:0"> statement combines two operations; it searches for the named module, then it binds the results of that search to a name in the local scope. The search operation of the </span><span data-offset-key="b687c57b822b479b92c23864ae514744:1">`import`</span><span data-offset-key="b687c57b822b479b92c23864ae514744:2"> statement is defined as a call to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="02bee2c0da204297bb8110d8c30a4cd9"><span data-offset-key="02bee2c0da204297bb8110d8c30a4cd9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="383a1b56aba645a082d99ebf195eb2d8"><span data-offset-key="383a1b56aba645a082d99ebf195eb2d8:0"> function, with the appropriate arguments. The return value of </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="be5c7fd92a484b57a57902b75632544a"><span data-offset-key="be5c7fd92a484b57a57902b75632544a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="9e3f1176c30c4178978c3adac0364b4a"><span data-offset-key="9e3f1176c30c4178978c3adac0364b4a:0"> is used to perform the name binding operation of the </span><span data-offset-key="9e3f1176c30c4178978c3adac0364b4a:1">`import`</span><span data-offset-key="9e3f1176c30c4178978c3adac0364b4a:2"> statement. See the </span><span data-offset-key="9e3f1176c30c4178978c3adac0364b4a:3">`import`</span><span data-offset-key="9e3f1176c30c4178978c3adac0364b4a:4"> statement for the exact details of that name binding operation.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="274900ca88d04866b99d2f4b3769383f"><span data-offset-key="274900ca88d04866b99d2f4b3769383f:0">A direct call to </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c4931eee4401446086086f3c388cb0f9"><span data-offset-key="c4931eee4401446086086f3c388cb0f9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e8eb3a7496c54557b8ad4080cc1b402d"><span data-offset-key="e8eb3a7496c54557b8ad4080cc1b402d:0"> performs only the module search and, if found, the module creation operation. While certain side-effects may occur, such as the importing of parent packages, and the updating of various caches (including </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.modules" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="eaddfa8dae594b06b6dccb0bcdf4882c"><span data-offset-key="eaddfa8dae594b06b6dccb0bcdf4882c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.modules</code></span></span></a><span data-key="d251b2bbbf80458a8a00b35301331e74"><span data-offset-key="d251b2bbbf80458a8a00b35301331e74:0">), only the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="64191e0fc43145ed8d7b5862ec2c5ce6"><span data-offset-key="64191e0fc43145ed8d7b5862ec2c5ce6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f8578a9861054c3b9db3a968e4671995"><span data-offset-key="f8578a9861054c3b9db3a968e4671995:0"> statement performs a name binding operation.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e3a5c1424eb2452ab3a5723289b26286"><span data-offset-key="e3a5c1424eb2452ab3a5723289b26286:0">When an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a3aeaa5718a94746880c41e823cabcc8"><span data-offset-key="a3aeaa5718a94746880c41e823cabcc8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e8fe3dfc5c1a4a2386b0b085c1a53ed7"><span data-offset-key="e8fe3dfc5c1a4a2386b0b085c1a53ed7:0"> statement is executed, the standard builtin </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="57116b6fea5e420995491613ef988616"><span data-offset-key="57116b6fea5e420995491613ef988616:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8bd7bb67a0b94f7590ca6ff469eef5c6"><span data-offset-key="8bd7bb67a0b94f7590ca6ff469eef5c6:0"> function is called. Other mechanisms for invoking the import system (such as </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#importlib.import_module" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ad54deac06df4eccbac4a43a3ce63e92"><span data-offset-key="ad54deac06df4eccbac4a43a3ce63e92:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib.import_module()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b36ac492bf7b40ca9cebe464efc61d8e"><span data-offset-key="b36ac492bf7b40ca9cebe464efc61d8e:0">) may choose to bypass </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4f9f731b1c2a4171a1ae1c627e0cfdba"><span data-offset-key="4f9f731b1c2a4171a1ae1c627e0cfdba:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="56e304e094e5492da2cb28a02d4c2774"><span data-offset-key="56e304e094e5492da2cb28a02d4c2774:0"> and use their own solutions to implement import semantics.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7bea2852657345e8a148ef4acf58051a"><span data-offset-key="7bea2852657345e8a148ef4acf58051a:0">When a module is first imported, Python searches for the module and if found, it creates a module object </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/import.html#fnmo" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f1aa88eca2794ec8aa3c221ca66bb1c1"><span data-offset-key="f1aa88eca2794ec8aa3c221ca66bb1c1:0">1</span></span></a><span data-key="2859af2838334d058659cd57af2f6be2"><span data-offset-key="2859af2838334d058659cd57af2f6be2:0">, initializing it. If the named module cannot be found, a </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ModuleNotFoundError" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3b076118dcbf4aaebcb0ce6653681e09"><span data-offset-key="3b076118dcbf4aaebcb0ce6653681e09:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">ModuleNotFoundError</code></span></span></a><span data-key="456c1cc938aa427598e61404a5b61004"><span data-offset-key="456c1cc938aa427598e61404a5b61004:0"> is raised. Python implements various strategies to search for the named module when the import machinery is invoked. These strategies can be modified and extended by using various hooks described in the sections below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="738f22e8e54d4ab7b3cc0e0f2b876eb0"><span data-offset-key="738f22e8e54d4ab7b3cc0e0f2b876eb0:0">Changed in version 3.3: The import system has been updated to fully implement the second phase of </span></span><a href="https://www.python.org/dev/peps/pep-0302" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0ce3793df47f4ee9877fa32d8029eeb6"><span data-offset-key="0ce3793df47f4ee9877fa32d8029eeb6:0"><strong>PEP 302</strong></span></span></a><span data-key="ee2749f8e02e40b2bb44966c26ab8a52"><span data-offset-key="ee2749f8e02e40b2bb44966c26ab8a52:0">. There is no longer any implicit import machinery - the full import system is exposed through </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.meta_path" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1dbb0718d7084c3e95183f8b2334a3de"><span data-offset-key="1dbb0718d7084c3e95183f8b2334a3de:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.meta_path</code></span></span></a><span data-key="66ccc7c00b364dada823a5fa71f2aa9b"><span data-offset-key="66ccc7c00b364dada823a5fa71f2aa9b:0">. In addition, native namespace package support has been implemented (see </span></span><a href="https://www.python.org/dev/peps/pep-0420" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3042b1ac6e1145c7bb563df9891e3221"><span data-offset-key="3042b1ac6e1145c7bb563df9891e3221:0"><strong>PEP 420</strong></span></span></a><span data-key="24f36106809a42cd9eda85454823cef8"><span data-offset-key="24f36106809a42cd9eda85454823cef8:0">).</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2c46d9a40ad547778bd64efd572d9935"><span data-offset-key="2c46d9a40ad547778bd64efd572d9935:0">5.1. </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#module-importlib" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ee483b72334f474eb3a1ba658ee0d413"><span data-offset-key="ee483b72334f474eb3a1ba658ee0d413:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib</code></span></span></a><span data-key="67468a5f7b724ab0ae46722237dc7002"><span data-offset-key="67468a5f7b724ab0ae46722237dc7002:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4d838f3118cc4e629bfa9ec55a71c1ae"><span data-offset-key="4d838f3118cc4e629bfa9ec55a71c1ae:0">The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#module-importlib" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="472901ba60de46298cbcf7587b8c4bc6"><span data-offset-key="472901ba60de46298cbcf7587b8c4bc6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a530f92406d946b8a1c88d8038f629ac"><span data-offset-key="a530f92406d946b8a1c88d8038f629ac:0"> module provides a rich API for interacting with the import system. For example </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#importlib.import_module" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e4d1263557134da19446626f9b03fb21"><span data-offset-key="e4d1263557134da19446626f9b03fb21:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib.import_module()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4bb206538e8f4a2eaffe242f7a35c2ab"><span data-offset-key="4bb206538e8f4a2eaffe242f7a35c2ab:0"> provides a recommended, simpler API than built-in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6f70640dfdfa46bea34469f55834d9b6"><span data-offset-key="6f70640dfdfa46bea34469f55834d9b6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="70bf75a0ebcd4442bd036761e359808c"><span data-offset-key="70bf75a0ebcd4442bd036761e359808c:0"> for invoking the import machinery. Refer to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#module-importlib" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e86c00faa453405fada64fbe9ac4125b"><span data-offset-key="e86c00faa453405fada64fbe9ac4125b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bb32d61d391146219508ded6b1726b6b"><span data-offset-key="bb32d61d391146219508ded6b1726b6b:0"> library documentation for additional detail.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3cdadd36f1644184bff711a9ac3dc3f0"><span data-offset-key="3cdadd36f1644184bff711a9ac3dc3f0:0">5.2. Packages</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f219518a5485447097ccc2cab6eef92a"><span data-offset-key="f219518a5485447097ccc2cab6eef92a:0">Python has only one type of module object, and all modules are of this type, regardless of whether the module is implemented in Python, C, or something else. To help organize modules and provide a naming hierarchy, Python has a concept of </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-package" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d89c53e18394449c8d941a7b04328c6a"><span data-offset-key="d89c53e18394449c8d941a7b04328c6a:0">packages</span></span></a><span data-key="99c47c2a9293417d89348c712779bdb9"><span data-offset-key="99c47c2a9293417d89348c712779bdb9:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0017d89349a44d33a8d7fa867a9b060f"><span data-offset-key="0017d89349a44d33a8d7fa867a9b060f:0">You can think of packages as the directories on a file system and modules as files within directories, but don’t take this analogy too literally since packages and modules need not originate from the file system. For the purposes of this documentation, we’ll use this convenient analogy of directories and files. Like file system directories, packages are organized hierarchically, and packages may themselves contain subpackages, as well as regular modules.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2a8fa54855ef45ffbab9f73811f0d2b0"><span data-offset-key="2a8fa54855ef45ffbab9f73811f0d2b0:0">It’s important to keep in mind that all packages are modules, but not all modules are packages. Or put another way, packages are just a special kind of module. Specifically, any module that contains a </span><span data-offset-key="2a8fa54855ef45ffbab9f73811f0d2b0:1">`__path__`</span><span data-offset-key="2a8fa54855ef45ffbab9f73811f0d2b0:2"> attribute is considered a package.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4b949a1f447b4c2ba29b5dad2791fc65"><span data-offset-key="4b949a1f447b4c2ba29b5dad2791fc65:0">All modules have a name. Subpackage names are separated from their parent package name by a dot, akin to Python’s standard attribute access syntax. Thus you might have a module called </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#module-sys" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e3b61ebf218a443ca5b7e75dc085259e"><span data-offset-key="e3b61ebf218a443ca5b7e75dc085259e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys</code></span></span></a><span data-key="00c9188aa3f240a69ef81da420573896"><span data-offset-key="00c9188aa3f240a69ef81da420573896:0"> and a package called </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/email.html#module-email" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c7724ae164c44d7ea8999113c6c78576"><span data-offset-key="c7724ae164c44d7ea8999113c6c78576:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">email</code></span></span></a><span data-key="16a5c0f87e634c40aa491d7545b220c8"><span data-offset-key="16a5c0f87e634c40aa491d7545b220c8:0">, which in turn has a subpackage called </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/email.mime.html#module-email.mime" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d7317fb21bc546f8b2ac28652629d8db"><span data-offset-key="d7317fb21bc546f8b2ac28652629d8db:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">email.mime</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e9a89f6b88cc48738f61d016d86251e5"><span data-offset-key="e9a89f6b88cc48738f61d016d86251e5:0"> and a module within that subpackage called </span><span data-offset-key="e9a89f6b88cc48738f61d016d86251e5:1">`email.mime.text`</span><span data-offset-key="e9a89f6b88cc48738f61d016d86251e5:2">.</span></span></span>

###

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4237c05c8f7540da806da488255ad46d"><span data-offset-key="4237c05c8f7540da806da488255ad46d:0">5.2.1. Regular packages</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cab1155962a546f39676e1561d527515"><span data-offset-key="cab1155962a546f39676e1561d527515:0">Python defines two types of packages, </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-regular-package" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4b77d505b395463b8e8372a0a8130ca5"><span data-offset-key="4b77d505b395463b8e8372a0a8130ca5:0">regular packages</span></span></a><span data-key="98f6dbf6b1b4425799db782f36fa8104"><span data-offset-key="98f6dbf6b1b4425799db782f36fa8104:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-namespace-package" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b4d7c4569aa94d4286cc68dd654042e4"><span data-offset-key="b4d7c4569aa94d4286cc68dd654042e4:0">namespace packages</span></span></a><span data-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e"><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:0">. Regular packages are traditional packages as they existed in Python 3.2 and earlier. A regular package is typically implemented as a directory containing an </span><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:1">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:2"> file. When a regular package is imported, this </span><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:3">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:4"> file is implicitly executed, and the objects it defines are bound to names in the package’s namespace. The </span><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:5">`__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="252da09d25794ad39da2520026b7cb5e:6"> file can contain the same Python code that any other module can contain, and Python will add some additional attributes to the module when it is imported.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cd7d210d65d04943baa530dd21475789"><span data-offset-key="cd7d210d65d04943baa530dd21475789:0">For example, the following file system layout defines a top level </span><span data-offset-key="cd7d210d65d04943baa530dd21475789:1">`parent`</span><span data-offset-key="cd7d210d65d04943baa530dd21475789:2"> package with three subpackages:</span></span></span>

    parent/    __init__.py    one/        __init__.py    two/        __init__.py    three/        __init__.py

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818"><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:0">Importing </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:1">`parent.one`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:2"> will implicitly execute </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:3">`parent/__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:5">`parent/one/__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:6">. Subsequent imports of </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:7">`parent.two`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:8"> or </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:9">`parent.three`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:10"> will execute </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:11">`parent/two/__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:12"> and </span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:13">`parent/three/__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="3f1618ce437d422581525d13937ad818:14"> respectively.</span></span></span>

###

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="371351101e01411dae40e509a2b34f90"><span data-offset-key="371351101e01411dae40e509a2b34f90:0">5.2.2. Namespace packages</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c44670ad04da4d2b9680248a83f0a82c"><span data-offset-key="c44670ad04da4d2b9680248a83f0a82c:0">A namespace package is a composite of various </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-portion" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7f90f3dc124f4910a7dd73e35ad04f2d"><span data-offset-key="7f90f3dc124f4910a7dd73e35ad04f2d:0">portions</span></span></a><span data-key="a9ee83f5032c4b70befc00ff6c4c171a"><span data-offset-key="a9ee83f5032c4b70befc00ff6c4c171a:0">, where each portion contributes a subpackage to the parent package. Portions may reside in different locations on the file system. Portions may also be found in zip files, on the network, or anywhere else that Python searches during import. Namespace packages may or may not correspond directly to objects on the file system; they may be virtual modules that have no concrete representation.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7d1582bbe21c4131ae1df8f0d34d8589"><span data-offset-key="7d1582bbe21c4131ae1df8f0d34d8589:0">Namespace packages do not use an ordinary list for their </span><span data-offset-key="7d1582bbe21c4131ae1df8f0d34d8589:1">`__path__`</span><span data-offset-key="7d1582bbe21c4131ae1df8f0d34d8589:2"> attribute. They instead use a custom iterable type which will automatically perform a new search for package portions on the next import attempt within that package if the path of their parent package (or </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.path" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="375d95a508044d49a0a1ce82cfb5b643"><span data-offset-key="375d95a508044d49a0a1ce82cfb5b643:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.path</code></span></span></a><span data-key="70041564754a4316871a16efea03abfe"><span data-offset-key="70041564754a4316871a16efea03abfe:0"> for a top level package) changes.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab"><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:0">With namespace packages, there is no </span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:1">`parent/__init__.py`</span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:2"> file. In fact, there may be multiple </span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:3">`parent`</span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:4"> directories found during import search, where each one is provided by a different portion. Thus </span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:5">`parent/one`</span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:6"> may not be physically located next to </span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:7">`parent/two`</span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:8">. In this case, Python will create a namespace package for the top-level </span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:9">`parent`</span><span data-offset-key="be21ad0fcc80417daf47683447179cab:10"> package whenever it or one of its subpackages is imported.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="837d461d080548fca06cb6eb7f5de26e"><span data-offset-key="837d461d080548fca06cb6eb7f5de26e:0">See also </span></span><a href="https://www.python.org/dev/peps/pep-0420" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8285864746084715b97e0e09c80c5d3c"><span data-offset-key="8285864746084715b97e0e09c80c5d3c:0"><strong>PEP 420</strong></span></span></a><span data-key="af99296e334146889a47385de2946f40"><span data-offset-key="af99296e334146889a47385de2946f40:0"> for the namespace package specification.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="132c3f4d660a458aa5df110933363e4c"><span data-offset-key="132c3f4d660a458aa5df110933363e4c:0">5.3. Searching</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e9749c48b4a5430495e564e0e98d5231"><span data-offset-key="e9749c48b4a5430495e564e0e98d5231:0">To begin the search, Python needs the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/glossary.html#term-qualified-name" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f3f1d182dfbd4c85ace0f5344d0819d6"><span data-offset-key="f3f1d182dfbd4c85ace0f5344d0819d6:0">fully qualified</span></span></a><span data-key="a1fb069b3d204f48abc00617ff920171"><span data-offset-key="a1fb069b3d204f48abc00617ff920171:0"> name of the module (or package, but for the purposes of this discussion, the difference is immaterial) being imported. This name may come from various arguments to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="38e544e8a35c4fa5823a1dfec9b53114"><span data-offset-key="38e544e8a35c4fa5823a1dfec9b53114:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7b1daef7028f40aa9e08f2a3d15b2fe5"><span data-offset-key="7b1daef7028f40aa9e08f2a3d15b2fe5:0"> statement, or from the parameters to the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#importlib.import_module" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a3fddbd9c334478a90681b408daca2e1"><span data-offset-key="a3fddbd9c334478a90681b408daca2e1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib.import_module()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ad4ee6a7f23f4620b87d267d0955a6b0"><span data-offset-key="ad4ee6a7f23f4620b87d267d0955a6b0:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#__import__" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a0262b68df8a40708bcaea2e400274e3"><span data-offset-key="a0262b68df8a40708bcaea2e400274e3:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">**import**()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ed5d99af62e34f18b5d6caf7fc5151d7"><span data-offset-key="ed5d99af62e34f18b5d6caf7fc5151d7:0"> functions.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4"><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:0">This name will be used in various phases of the import search, and it may be the dotted path to a submodule, e.g. </span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:1">`foo.bar.baz`</span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:2">. In this case, Python first tries to import </span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:3">`foo`</span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:4">, then </span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:5">`foo.bar`</span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:6">, and finally </span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:7">`foo.bar.baz`</span><span data-offset-key="163039e9e05b4779b2591d40d6f91ab4:8">. If any of the intermediate imports fail, a </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ModuleNotFoundError" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ad810b1ede824673b03367dcc3e2a402"><span data-offset-key="ad810b1ede824673b03367dcc3e2a402:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">ModuleNotFoundError</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ea7c033839964926b71ca7c3980d6716"><span data-offset-key="ea7c033839964926b71ca7c3980d6716:0"> is raised.</span></span></span>

###

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5d4ce21060db4d14a63e3f421bb33fe8"><span data-offset-key="5d4ce21060db4d14a63e3f421bb33fe8:0">5.3.1. The module cache</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="176c42ee9b42420b84a4acbbf25c7b1e"><span data-offset-key="176c42ee9b42420b84a4acbbf25c7b1e:0">The first place checked during import search is </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.modules" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7061dfefd8fa48d5b427a2ad7c1b898c"><span data-offset-key="7061dfefd8fa48d5b427a2ad7c1b898c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.modules</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bd031406ed034aada89e4b0bd70056bf"><span data-offset-key="bd031406ed034aada89e4b0bd70056bf:0">. This mapping serves as a cache of all modules that have been previously imported, including the intermediate paths. So if </span><span data-offset-key="bd031406ed034aada89e4b0bd70056bf:1">`foo.bar.baz`</span><span data-offset-key="bd031406ed034aada89e4b0bd70056bf:2"> was previously imported, </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.modules" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b1bf2eabe00240b886771157a7ba75a5"><span data-offset-key="b1bf2eabe00240b886771157a7ba75a5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.modules</code></span></span></a><span data-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f"><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:0"> will contain entries for </span><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:1">`foo`</span><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:2">, </span><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:3">`foo.bar`</span><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:4">, and </span><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:5">`foo.bar.baz`</span><span data-offset-key="de75c7d635ac40ae872425fc60263e7f:6">. Each key will have as its value the corresponding module object.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d7675dc08d24ecc8969454e34edab59"><span data-offset-key="1d7675dc08d24ecc8969454e34edab59:0">During import, the module name is looked up in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.modules" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d5d3ee4ad4654d14ab4f1e02b4be7de4"><span data-offset-key="d5d3ee4ad4654d14ab4f1e02b4be7de4:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.modules</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4f5f4136207e46cdb1eb437dd9629799"><span data-offset-key="4f5f4136207e46cdb1eb437dd9629799:0"> and if present, the associated value is the module satisfying the import, and the process completes. However, if the value is </span><span data-offset-key="4f5f4136207e46cdb1eb437dd9629799:1">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="4f5f4136207e46cdb1eb437dd9629799:2">, then a </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ModuleNotFoundError" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3e2e57ed689a4de5993464230a0c37b4"><span data-offset-key="3e2e57ed689a4de5993464230a0c37b4:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">ModuleNotFoundError</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b68e711dd95845f8a3f09d86a5ebd5fc"><span data-offset-key="b68e711dd95845f8a3f09d86a5ebd5fc:0"> is raised. If the module name is missing, Python will continue searching for the module.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3f7b700d47d74f80a645065778eaea6d"><span data-offset-key="3f7b700d47d74f80a645065778eaea6d:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.modules" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="63de2047b4ad45489d3561f4c6145d2d"><span data-offset-key="63de2047b4ad45489d3561f4c6145d2d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.modules</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2d17f456be044db5931ad0f0add8c252"><span data-offset-key="2d17f456be044db5931ad0f0add8c252:0"> is writable. Deleting a key may not destroy the associated module (as other modules may hold references to it), but it will invalidate the cache entry for the named module, causing Python to search anew for the named module upon its next import. The key can also be assigned to </span><span data-offset-key="2d17f456be044db5931ad0f0add8c252:1">`None`</span><span data-offset-key="2d17f456be044db5931ad0f0add8c252:2">, forcing the next import of the module to result in a </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#ModuleNotFoundError" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c34ffa1092e34965bbad388d6ecbc533"><span data-offset-key="c34ffa1092e34965bbad388d6ecbc533:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">ModuleNotFoundError</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7d4a7022c419451bb9930e641016d440"><span data-offset-key="7d4a7022c419451bb9930e641016d440:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e37c720b1872458fa4c5013b65549410"><span data-offset-key="e37c720b1872458fa4c5013b65549410:0">Beware though, as if you keep a reference to the module object, invalidate its cache entry in </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/sys.html#sys.modules" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3c8bca42f0c74d45b4fbd55ad0385f06"><span data-offset-key="3c8bca42f0c74d45b4fbd55ad0385f06:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">sys.modules</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7077742d50384da79ca451577a798153"><span data-offset-key="7077742d50384da79ca451577a798153:0">, and then re-import the named module, the two module objects will </span><span data-offset-key="7077742d50384da79ca451577a798153:1">_not_</span><span data-offset-key="7077742d50384da79ca451577a798153:2"> be the same. By contrast, </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/importlib.html#importlib.reload" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d39b6097929841738894792cb06b4c55"><span data-offset-key="d39b6097929841738894792cb06b4c55:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">importlib.reload()</code></span></span></a><span data-key="58f0f8ea38414b87bd2577f1678283cd"><span data-offset-key="58f0f8ea38414b87bd2577f1678283cd:0"> will reuse the </span><span data-offset-key="58f0f8ea38414b87bd2577f1678283cd:1">_same_</span><span data-offset-key="58f0f8ea38414b87bd2577f1678283cd:2"> module object, and simply reinitialise the module contents by rerunning the module’s code.</span></span></span>

###
